World Games Delegation Travelogue (Letter 7) by Special Correspondent Feng Youzhen from the Central News Agency 179

(35) A Day in Venice

At 11 PM on the 20th, the postal ship arrived in Venice. After a simple welcome reception on the ship, we disembarked at 12:15 AM and stepped onto the European continent. There was a road in front of the pier. We marched for two or three hundred steps to a small pier, where a special ship carried us to three hotels for lodging. It was already 2:30 AM.

Venice is a world-renowned water city. The entire city is built entirely on water. Except for the sidewalks and a few streets in front of the houses, the rest is all waterways connected by bridges. It is estimated that there are more than 150 canals and more than 400 bridges in the city. When the special ship was moving forward in a large river, the whole city had already fallen asleep, quiet and silent. The lights reflected in the green river water, forming curved lines. The beauty of the scenery evoked infinite aesthetic feelings in people. The night in Venice is truly intoxicating and unforgettable.

Germany prepared three special carriages to welcome us to Venice. Originally scheduled to depart at 7 AM on the 21st, but because the ship arrived late and everyone was too tired from the journey, it was postponed for one day. Therefore, we were able to tour Venice for a day.

In this famous water city, we could not find a car to use as a means of transportation. Instead, there were shuttling steamboats or gondolas rowed by two people with pointed bows and sterns.

At 10 AM on the 21st, everyone took a steamboat to visit St. Mark's Church and the Ducal Palace. When we got off the steamboat and walked to the square in front of these two great and solemn buildings, we couldn't help but feel a sense of solemnity. Countless pigeons were parked on the square. They were not afraid of tourists at all. And if you spent a few cents to buy a bag of corn on a small stall and hold it in your hand, a group of pigeons would compete to fly onto your arm to eat, which was extremely interesting.

St. Mark's Church was built to commemorate Mark, the disciple of Jesus. It is said that his tomb is buried under the church. This building is a relic of the 11th century and can be called solemn and magnificent. Walking inside, the dimness easily makes people with religious beliefs feel a sense of mystery. The Ducal Palace is the palace of the Venetian kingdom in the Middle Ages. It is a four-story building that was expanded over the years from the 13th century to the 16th century. The scope is very grand. Now that the Venetian kingdom has long been destroyed, the Venice city government has preserved this palace as a precious historical site. People who go in to visit have to pay twelve lira (each lira is about equal to 30 cents in our currency). Because we were a group, we only paid half price. The palace displays stone statues of leaders of past dynasties. The carvings are extremely exquisite. All the walls and ceilings are painted with precious oil paintings. The brushwork is magnificent and extremely delicate. Italian sculpture and painting occupy a very important position in Western art. Here, you can see their spirit to some extent. Two exhibition rooms display many weapons from the Middle Ages, including knives, swords, and spears, in great variety. There are also several helmets and armor, from head to toe, all made of pure steel, fully demonstrating the martial spirit of the warriors of that era. Two machine guns from the early 16th century were also on display. Each had ten barrels. When used, gunpowder was loaded into the muzzle, and then the mechanism was used to fire them one by one. After four centuries of evolution, the weapons of killing are no longer the same as they were then.

The attendant in the weapons exhibition room specially led us to see the chastity belt displayed in the glass cabinet. It is said that when warriors in the Middle Ages went on expeditions, they were afraid that their wives would commit adultery, so they used steel to cast chastity belts. The shape is like the sanitary napkins used by modern ladies, with only two thorn-like small holes left for the female genitals and anus. The authority of warriors in the male-centered era over women can be imagined from this.

It is said that the Venetian kingdom was actually a republican political system. The king was elected by the people. It was a lifelong position, but it was not passed down to his children. There is a conference hall that is 165 feet long and 75 feet wide, which can accommodate 1,600 people. It is said that it was where kings of past dynasties convened meetings of nobles. The walls are painted with portraits of kings of past dynasties, and the ceiling is painted with a portrait of a queen, which can express a solemn expression. There are five or six more small conference halls, and the layout is roughly the same.

At around 1 PM, we returned to the hotel for lunch. Suddenly, dark clouds gathered and it started to rain heavily. The players, tired and exhausted, took this opportunity to rest in the hotel. When the rain stopped and the sky cleared, it was already sunset. The bells of dozens of churches in the city came one after another, shrouding this beautiful water city in a mysterious atmosphere. Some of the players gathered in groups of three or five, sitting in gondolas and rippling in the blue waves. Some strolled leisurely through the streets and alleys. Some sat in the small garden in front of the hotel listening to the band playing. Italian music is unique in the European music scene. The bands of five or six people organized in Venetian hotels and cafes are everywhere. The tunes are melodious and the tones are elegant, which is rare to hear in the country. After a hard day's work, people of middle or higher standing buy a cup of coffee or a cold drink and sit quietly to enjoy it (without dancing). It can be said that they are packed to the rafters, which shows their strong interest in music. Because we were leaving early the next morning, the players had all gone to sleep in this quiet water city before 10 PM.

Education News

Shanghai Education Bureau Ordered to Hold General Examinations; Announces Regulations for Six Types of Examinations 180

The Shanghai Education Bureau was ordered to hold general examinations and, in accordance with the Examination Law, published regulations for six types of examinations, as follows:

(1) Regulations for the General Examination for General Administrative Personnel

Article 1: The general examination for general administrative personnel shall be conducted in accordance with these regulations, unless otherwise provided by law.

Article 2: Nationals of the Republic of China who possess one of the following qualifications may take the general examination for general administrative personnel: 1. Graduation from a public or registered private senior middle school (old system) or other equivalent school with a certificate; 2. Passing a qualification examination for equivalent academic ability to graduation from the schools listed in the preceding paragraph; 3. Graduation from a public or Ministry of Education-registered or recognized domestic or foreign school with one year or more of specialized study and a certificate; 4. Qualification to take the higher examination; 5. Having served in an administrative agency for three years or more with documentary evidence.

Article 3: The subjects of the first examination are as follows: 1. Chinese essay and official documents; 2. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings: The Three Principles of the People and the National Reconstruction Program; 3. Chinese history and geography; 4. Constitution (Before the promulgation of the Constitution, the Provisional Constitution of the Republic of China during the Period of Political Tutelage will be tested).

Article 4: The subjects of the second examination are as follows: 1. Administrative law; 2. Outline of civil law; 3. Outline of criminal law; 4. Local autonomy regulations; 5. Economics.

Article 5: The third examination shall consist of an interview with the examinee on the subjects of the second examination and his/her experience.

Article 6: These regulations shall come into force on the date of promulgation.

(2) Amended Regulations for the General Examination for Educational Administrative Personnel

Article 1: The general examination for educational administrative personnel shall be conducted in accordance with these regulations, unless otherwise provided by law.

Article 2: Nationals of the Republic of China who possess one of the following qualifications may take the general examination for educational administrative personnel: 1. Graduation from a public or registered private normal school, senior middle school (old system), or other equivalent school with a certificate; 2. Passing a qualification examination for equivalent academic ability to graduation from the schools listed in the preceding paragraph; 3. Qualification to take the higher examination; 4. Having served in an educational administrative agency for three years or more with documentary evidence; 5. Having served as a teacher or staff member in a senior elementary school or higher for three years or more with documentary evidence.

Article 3: The subjects of the first examination are as follows: 1. Chinese essay and official documents; 2. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings: The Three Principles of the People and the National Reconstruction Program; 3. Chinese history and geography; 4. Constitution (Before the promulgation of the Constitution, the Provisional Constitution of the Republic of China during the Period of Political Tutelage will be tested).

Article 4: The subjects of the second examination are as follows: A. Required subjects: 1. Principles of education; 2. Educational administration and educational laws and regulations; 3. Outline of school inspection; 4. Outline of civil law. B. Elective subjects: 1. Educational psychology; 2. Sociology; 3. Educational systems of various countries; 4. Educational statistics. Choose one of the above elective subjects.

Article 5: The third examination shall consist of an interview with the examinee on the required subjects of the second examination and his/her experience.

Article 6: These regulations shall come into force on the date of promulgation.

(3) Regulations for the General Examination for Financial Administrative Personnel

Article 1: The general examination for financial administrative personnel shall be conducted in accordance with these regulations, unless otherwise provided by law.

Article 2: Nationals of the Republic of China who possess one of the following qualifications may take the general examination for financial administrative personnel: 1. Graduation from a public or registered private senior middle school (old system) or other equivalent school with a certificate; 2. Passing a qualification examination for equivalent academic ability to graduation from the schools listed in the preceding paragraph; 3. Graduation from a public or Ministry of Education-registered or recognized domestic or foreign school with one year or more of specialized study in finance, economics, commerce, accounting, banking, law, or politics and a certificate; 4. Qualification to take the higher examination; 5. Having served in a financial agency for three years or more with documentary evidence.

Article 3: The subjects of the first examination are as follows: 1. Chinese essay and official documents; 2. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings: The Three Principles of the People and the National Reconstruction Program; 3. Chinese history and geography; 4. Constitution (Before the promulgation of the Constitution, the Provisional Constitution of the Republic of China during the Period of Political Tutelage will be tested).

Article 4: The subjects of the second examination are as follows: 1. Economics; 2. Public finance; 3. Government accounting; 4. Financial laws and regulations; 5. Outline of civil law.

Article 5: The third examination shall consist of an interview with the examinee on the subjects of economics, public finance, and financial laws and regulations from the second examination, and his/her experience.

Article 6: These regulations shall come into force on the date of promulgation.

(4) Amended Regulations for the General Examination for Police Administrative Personnel

Article 1: The general examination for police administrative personnel shall be conducted in accordance with these regulations, unless otherwise provided by law.

Article 2: Nationals of the Republic of China who possess one of the following qualifications may take the general examination for police administrative personnel: 1. Graduation from a public or registered private senior middle school (old system) or other equivalent school with a certificate; 2. Passing a qualification examination for equivalent academic ability to graduation from the schools listed in the preceding paragraph; 3. Graduation from a public or Ministry of Education-registered or recognized domestic or foreign police, military, law, or political school with one year or more of specialized study and a certificate; 4. Qualification to take the higher examination; 5. Having served as a commissioned officer or equivalent position in a police agency for one year or more, or having served in a police agency for three years or more with documentary evidence.

Article 3: The subjects of the first examination are as follows: 1. Chinese essay and official documents; 2. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings: The Three Principles of the People and the National Reconstruction Program; 3. Chinese history and geography; 4. Constitution (Before the promulgation of the Constitution, the Provisional Constitution of the Republic of China during the Period of Political Tutelage will be tested).

Article 4: The subjects of the second examination are as follows: 1. Police science; 2. Regulations on violations of police law and duty essentials; 3. Household registration law; 4. Local autonomy regulations; 5. Outline of civil and criminal law.

Article 5: The third examination shall consist of an interview with the examinee on the subjects of the second examination and his/her experience.

Article 6: These regulations shall come into force on the date of promulgation. (To be continued)

Foreign Faculty Members Employed by National Institutions of Higher Education 184

The Ministry of Education has compiled statistics on the number and monthly salaries of foreign faculty members in all schools above the specialized college level throughout the country for the 23rd academic year, based on materials collected from these schools. The main points are as follows: (1) "Number of Faculty Members": National universities, colleges, and specialized colleges have a total of 137 faculty members, public specialized colleges have 5, provincial universities and colleges have 20, and private universities, colleges, and specialized colleges have 542. The total is 704. (598 teachers, 106 staff members). (2) "Monthly Salaries of Faculty Members": National universities, colleges, and specialized colleges: 48,338 yuan; public specialized colleges: 1,250 yuan; provincial universities and colleges: 3,759 yuan; private universities, colleges, and specialized colleges: 115,447 yuan. The total is 166,294 yuan (142,046 yuan for teachers, 24,248 yuan for staff members). (3) "Comparison of Teachers' Monthly Salaries": "National Universities": highest salary 1,100 yuan, colleges 870 yuan, specialized colleges 400 yuan; lowest salary universities 50 yuan, colleges 120 yuan, specialized colleges 280 yuan. "Public Specialized Colleges": highest salary 450 yuan, lowest salary 320 yuan. "Provincial Universities": highest salary 825 yuan, specialized colleges 583 yuan; lowest salary universities 300 yuan, colleges 120 yuan. "Private Universities": highest salary 1,350 yuan, colleges 600 yuan, specialized colleges 250 yuan; lowest salary universities 80 yuan, colleges 100 yuan. (4) "Comparison of Staff Members' Monthly Salaries": "National Universities": highest salary 1,000 yuan, colleges 600 yuan; lowest salary universities 150 yuan, colleges 175 yuan. "Public Specialized Colleges": monthly salary 350 yuan. "Private Universities": highest salary 720 yuan, colleges 400 yuan; lowest salary fire 80 yuan, colleges 150 yuan.

(Explanation) (1) Among the 704 foreign faculty members, teachers from the United States, Germany, and France are the most numerous. In universities, there are 227 American teachers (146 men, 81 women), 72 German teachers (men, 10 women), and 65 French teachers (63 men, 2 women). In colleges, there are 10 Western American teachers (46 men, 58 women), 4 German teachers, and 22 French teachers (21 men). In specialized colleges, there are 5 American teachers (4 men), 3 German teachers (1 man), and 1 French teacher (woman). The next largest group is British teachers, with 54 in universities, 17 in colleges, and 1 in specialized colleges. The next largest group is Japanese teachers, with 14 in universities, 9 in colleges, and 13 in specialized colleges. There are also 51 Canadian teachers and 16 Australian teachers. In addition, there are foreign teachers from Switzerland, Sweden, Belgium, Holland, Italy, the Czech Republic, Spain, Australia, the Philippines, Singapore, Korea, Taiwan, and other places, with one, two, three, or four teachers in universities, colleges, and specialized colleges. (2) The difference between the highest and lowest monthly salaries of foreign faculty members is very large. Generally, the former are specially hired by our side, and the latter are mostly already in China with considerable positions and do not teach for the purpose of making a living. For example, Ms. Ya Aining, a German female teacher at Zhejiang University, teaches in China with her husband, Professor Ya Aier. She does not teach as a way of life, so she teaches very little, and her salary is only 50 yuan per month, it is said.

Municipal Education Bureau Regularly Implements Lung Examinations for Teachers and Staff in All Schools; From September 1st to October 30th, the Examinations Will Be Conducted by the China Anti-Tuberculosis Association 185

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau instructed all levels of schools in the city, stating: "The bureau has approved a letter from the China Anti-Tuberculosis Association, stating that tuberculosis is rampant and harmful to young people, especially the spread of tuberculosis in elementary schools, which is even more alarming. It has been found that the infection of tuberculosis in children is mostly acquired through contact with infected adults. Therefore, the health of elementary school teachers is closely related to students. For preventive purposes, the association plans to first conduct X-ray lung examinations for elementary school teachers in the city and, for the purpose of promotion, charge only one yuan per person for the procedure. The bureau has always attached great importance to school hygiene and the health of teachers and students. Therefore, we are sending this special letter, hoping that you will adopt it. The bureau believes that preventing tuberculosis is indeed necessary, and all teachers and staff in schools at all levels in the city should undergo examinations. It is hereby decided that from September 1st to October 30th of this year, every Monday, Tuesday, Thursday, and Friday from 9:00 AM to 10:30 AM, principals should prepare letters and go to the Hygiene Office on Fangxie Road, Linyin Road in the Nanshi District for examinations. Each time, the number of people should not exceed 50. This order is hereby issued to all schools for compliance."

Comparison of Chinese and American Secondary Education 186

Dr. Shen Yizhen Lectures at Provincial Shanghai High School: Mr. Shen Yizhen served as the Dean of Studies and Director of Guidance at Provincial Shanghai High School for seven years. He has profound research and rich experience in educational topics. He went to the United States on New Year's Day in 1932 to study education at Columbia University and obtained a doctorate. He arrived in Shanghai on the "Empress of Japan" on the evening of August 11th. On the afternoon of the 12th, he lectured on "Comparison of Chinese and American Secondary Education" at the summer school of Provincial Shanghai High School. After Mr. Wang Dagan, director of the summer school, delivered an introductory speech, Mr. Shen began his lecture, briefly listing four differences between Chinese and American secondary education: (1) Secondary education opportunities are universal in the United States, while only a few outstanding young people in China can enter middle school to study. (2) General secondary schools in the United States are all day schools, while most in China adopt a boarding system. (3) The physical health and mental vitality of secondary school students in the United States are unmatched by Chinese students. (4) Secondary schools in the United States pay great attention to educational and vocational guidance and can realize the ideal of "teaching students according to their aptitude." Dr. Shen cited examples and provided explanations, which were extremely brilliant. He was full of energy when he lectured and spoke eloquently. The audience was deeply moved. However, due to limited time and the fact that the audience was composed of students who had graduated from junior high school or elementary school, he did not fully elaborate. Finally, Principal Zheng delivered a speech and instructions, and the meeting adjourned at six o'clock.

Municipal Education Bureau Does Not Issue Regulations for Employment Training Classes 187

The Municipal Education Bureau previously received instructions from the Ministry of Education to hold employment training classes for graduates of schools above the specialized college level in the capital city, enrolling 1,000 graduates of domestic and foreign schools above the specialized college level in the most recent three years, providing them with short-term training, and assigning them work according to their scores after passing the practical examination. The bureau then forwarded the instructions and made public announcements in various newspapers. It is now known that graduates of domestic schools above the specialized college level are recommended by their original schools, and graduates of foreign schools are recommended by the Ministry of Education. All students in this city who request to attend the classes should directly contact their original schools or the Ministry of Education themselves. The Municipal Education Bureau will not issue any regulations on their behalf, it is said.

New Family and Hygiene

— Edited by Dr. Shen Zhaoquan

Health for Women: A Lifelong Issue 201

— Dr. Yao Shinian, Obstetrics and Gynecology Hospital, Hongkou

Sufficient health can make a woman more lovable. Every woman wants to be attractive because she wants the charm that every woman should have. Therefore, the prerequisite is health.

Sparkling eyes, rosy lips, and smooth complexion all clearly indicate that the body has received the nutrition of a special blood quality. All these beauty aids are enough to increase natural attractiveness…

The kind of frail woman who used to be loved by men in the past is now a relic of a bygone era and is no longer favored by modern men.

Sickly women no longer have the power to attract men today. What they want are spirited, energetic, and healthy women. They have realized that disease not only hinders the happiness of married life, but also prevents romantic life from being enjoyable and fulfilling.

To maintain feminine health and beauty, one must pay attention to hygiene. Special attention should be paid to hygiene during menstruation. Neglecting hygiene can cause many diseases. Irregular menstruation and leukorrhea are the most common and distressing ailments for women. They must be treated immediately without delay!

The desire for sexual activity is expressed by menstruation. Although the entity that induces sexual activity is hidden and invisible, monthly menstruation reveals the fluctuations of sexual love to women. This is an undeniable physiological phenomenon.

Since menstruation is a sign of a woman's health and a manifestation of her ability to create life, it should not be defiled or belittled. However, many women suffer from irregular menstruation, a tragic phenomenon that proves the uterus is unhealthy…

A woman with a healthy uterus and regular menstruation, no matter how ugly, has at least secured one aspect of feminine beauty. If the uterus is unhealthy, then irregular menstruation will naturally occur, such as too little or too much menstrual flow, early or late periods, amenorrhea, or painful menstruation. In addition to abdominal pain before and after menstruation, there may also be foul-smelling leukorrhea and bloody discharge, leading to weight loss, mental decline, and a host of diseases, turning her into a melancholy and sickly woman. How can such a woman be loved by men?

Pleasure and contentment derived from love are the most attractive elements in family life. Therefore, those frail ladies should quickly seek the path to health and not live a life of sadness and suffering!

According to clinical reports from world-renowned doctors, "Menorrin" is an important value in women's health products. Menorrin treatment has specific effects on qi and blood deficiency, irregular menstruation, leukorrhea, uterine atrophy, and neurasthenia, and for women without sickness to maintain health and beautiful appearance so that even after middle age, their youth can be preserved.

Abundant vitality is an invaluable treasure for a woman who wants to obtain feminine charm - "Menorrin" is the source of women's health, a holy medicine for solving pain.

Misconceptions about Gonorrhea

Reasons Why Gonorrhea is Difficult to Cure 202

— Dr. Zhang Yuanzhen

—Methods for Complete Eradication—

The difficulty of curing gonorrhea is a common lament among the medical community and patients alike. There are many reasons why it is difficult to cure. First, the acute symptoms of gonorrhea have passed and become chronic. In the chronic stage, the patient no longer feels pain and is unwilling to continue treatment for complete eradication. This is due to the patient's lack of patience. Second, the patient does not understand the principles of health maintenance. Third is the economic problem, the inability to seek medical treatment for a long time. Fourth is the nature of their occupation. In addition to the reasons mentioned above, there is also the most significant reason: there are many mucous glands along the urethra. It is difficult to eliminate the gonococci lurking deep within these mucous gland ducts. Therefore, gonorrhea that appears to have been cured on the surface can recur due to various triggers such as fatigue, sexual activity, and alcohol consumption. Child Health Care 206

— Written by Dr. Xu Shengzhang of the Shanghai Haining Road and Kenning Road Citizen Sanatorium

Parents protect their beloved children... How to prevent summer dangers...

Bacillary Dysentery and Epidemic Dysentery

Epidemic dysentery is the most dangerous disease among children, caused by eating uncooked fruits or spoiled food. This disease is most common in children aged three to six years, and is almost non-existent in breastfed babies.

Sudden high fever with cold hands and feet, falling into a coma, is epidemic dysentery; blood in the stool is bacillary dysentery. These are caused by the mischief of bacillary and epidemic dysentery bacteria. Bacillary dysentery is characterized by initial diarrhea and fever, followed by bloody stools with mucus. The average mortality rate is 16 to 30%, and it is even more dangerous in children.

Epidemic dysentery starts with abdominal pain, headache, vomiting, and a slight fever, followed by diarrhea. After a few hours, a high fever of 40 degrees or higher suddenly develops, and the patient immediately falls into a coma. Severe cases can die within a day of onset. Prevention: First, pay attention to food and drink, and do not eat raw or cold things. Flies are also carriers of bacillary and epidemic dysentery, so attention must be paid to prevent flies from landing on tableware and food. Special care should be taken when giving children cookies or fruits.

If you see that your child is dull—inactive—lacking energy, restless, has abdominal distension, diarrhea, vomiting, and a slight fever, you should quickly take "Di Chang Li" medicine Dys-etrin Tab. This can often eliminate disasters invisibly. This is the first condition to protect your beloved child from dying from epidemic dysentery. Generally, children have food accumulation and are prone to indigestion and stomach diseases, so taking "Di Chang Li" clears undigested substances in the intestinal tract, inhibits the activity of harmful putrefactive bacteria in the intestine, and can also promote the physiological functions of the stomach and intestines, strengthening the stomach and promoting digestion, and increasing nutrition. Therefore, taking this medicine has only benefits and no harm. Those who want to protect their beloved children should not take it lightly.

Shen Bao Literary Supplement

Reunion 228

— Yao Mu

Alone, lodging in a teeming metropolis, would I, having been immersed in the warmth of friends, feel a little estranged even if not lonely?

One day, the shadow of a former Japanese classmate suddenly surfaced in my memory. He said he had returned to his country ten years ago, and in these long years, we had corresponded two or three times before our communication ceased. I only heard from others that he had once attempted poetic suicide, and eventually married a geisha, but poetry remained his life's purpose and means. "Perhaps he is still in Tokyo? Perhaps he has already become a famous poet? It should be easy to find him." I thought. After that, when I was spending time in bookstores, I paid attention to the contents of literary magazines. Sure enough, in a newly published magazine, I found his work, still poetry, and as wonderfully strange as before. I immediately wrote a letter filled with humor and enthusiasm and sent it to the magazine. I waited with curiosity and anticipated joy. One day passed, two days passed, but he didn't come, and I didn't receive his reply. I thought the magazine had thrown my letter into the wastebasket.

On the fourth day, as usual, I had a simple lunch outside and returned to my apartment. As I passed through the reception room, a strange person suddenly stood up and called my name. I was startled. Upon closer inspection, this person was the Japanese friend I had been looking forward to. He had grown a small, brown-yellow mustache on his thick lips, and his hair was still a tangled mess of grass.

"Still 'manufacturing' poetry, as decadent as ever?" I couldn't help but bring back the words we used to tease each other with.

He smiled in agreement, and then we talked about our lives since we parted. I learned that he had indeed married and was the father of three children.

"Poetry is worthless here, and I can't produce more than two or three poems a month, so I have to work as a journalist." These words, coming from the mouth of a true poet, carried the bitter taste of real life.

Then he asked about the recent situations of the old classmates he remembered, and his conclusion was: "They have all become big shots!"

"Precisely where we can look down on them." I added. "But, why mention them? Do you still remember the girl from 渡　　家 you praised?" I teased him.

He couldn't help but laugh.

"I often dream of the scenery of × City. I remember writing a poem about the coolies coming out of the public toilet on the seaside avenue."

Our conversation completely immersed in memories of the past, and the innocent, uninhibited life of our youth vividly reappeared before my eyes.

At that time, I was also writing poetry, intentionally writing decadent and pure poetry. *Flowers of Evil* became my archetype, and the works of minor masters such as Rossetti and Swinburne, with their medieval melancholic undertones, were also what I enjoyed. The strictly controlled morning glory and the bat's daydream were the places where my imagination roamed. In action, I naturally indulged in the excitement and melancholy caused by women and wine.

However, in the hypocritical, shallow, Americanized school environment, this behavior was naturally seen as heresy, and my friends were limited. This Japanese friend, however, still got along with me. His disheveled hair, the mess of books and dirty clothes piled everywhere in his bedroom, and his somnambulistic strolling on campus late at night were just part of his poetic life. However, what impressed me the most was his love of poetry and his poetic customs. He was always "manufacturing" poetry, even if it was just manual manufacturing. Japanese poetry originally has a strange charm, and his imagination was even more extraordinarily strange, using words and expressions outside of poetic conventions. Although his poetry also had a morbid quality, his observation was keen and multifaceted, and it carried a slight satire. His themes were readily available. Children urinating on the road, garbage heaps, his own boots, and lampposts could all be used to make poetry. But it is precisely from this that we can glimpse the human and social flavor of his poetry.

As a result of associating with him, chatting and strolling together, I gradually came under his influence and felt that my poetry was too imitative and too self-centered. I also began to change my style. Unfortunately, he soon returned to Japan, and I, because of changes in my life, almost became disconnected from poetry. His influence ultimately did not produce much effect.

Immersed in such memories of the past, the embers of our friendship reignited. I promised to visit his home in a few days for a long talk and to meet his wife.

One drizzly morning, I finally found his home with some difficulty. Inside a small one-and-a-half-story, six-mat house, a woman wearing a white apron was tidying up the house, and two somewhat dirty-faced boys were playing at the door, but my friend had not yet gotten up.

"I'm sorry, I drank too much last night, and I didn't go to bed until [late o'clock]." After waiting for a long time, my friend finally came out with a sleepy face. He took me upstairs, we talked for a while, and then the woman who had been downstairs brought up tea and sweets, giving me a deep Japanese-style bow. Through his introduction, I learned that she was his wife. Traces of youthful beauty seemed to remain between her fair eyebrows, but the wrinkles on her forehead and at the corners of her eyes were like brands of excessive childbirth and labor, making her appearance seem older than her age. However, what surprised me the most was the rather desolate four walls and the empty bookshelf with few books. As I reached out to flip through his books on the bookshelf, he seemed to guess my doubts.

"Most of the books are in the pawnshop, what's left here is just what can't be pawned," he explained to me with a smile.

"Can books be pawned here? That's really great!" Our topic then shifted elsewhere. After eating the bananas that he had especially asked his wife to buy back, I said goodbye. However, "poet...wine...books...pawnshop...three children..." still linger in my mind.

Wang Zhanfu Enters the City 229

— Li

It has been about three or four days since Wang Zhanfu arrived in this ancient city. He finds everything interesting. He is grateful to have a relative living in the city; otherwise, he would never have had such an opportunity, and his life would simply have ended in the countryside. His relative, who runs a small business in the city, planned to invite him to stay in the city for a few days and enjoy the sights. The letter described all sorts of exciting things happening in the city, which stirred his stagnant heart. He sent a reply, telling his relative that he would set off immediately. After saving up enough money for expenses and pocket money, he chose a sunny day, abandoned his farm work, and, with a joyful heart, happily boarded a train directly to the city. In the three or four days since arriving in the city, he had spent every day strolling through the streets, admiring the scenery, and observing the lives of the city people.

That day, he was idly wandering along the street, gazing in a daze at the various goods in the shop windows, listening intently to the radio broadcasts, and finding it all very interesting. Trams, cars, horse carriages, rickshaws, and all sorts of pedestrians seemed to be talking to him. He was so absorbed in looking and listening that he completely forgot to move his feet. After a while, he grabbed a vendor, secretly took out two large coins, as if afraid of being seen, bought two pieces of hard candy, and blushed as he stuffed them into his mouth. Just as he was savoring the taste, a crowd of people nearby caught his attention. After watching for a while, he sensed that something interesting must be going on. Wanting to broaden his horizons, he rushed over without hesitation.

Several people were arguing in a group, seemingly over something that couldn't be resolved. He looked closely and saw that one person was holding a piece of paper, waving it in front of others, and repeatedly saying, "No, no, this price is unacceptable. It's too low. If you're sincere, add a little more."

Wang Zhanfu recognized it as a pawn ticket. He didn't understand the underlying principles, but he guessed there must be a story behind it. Soon, he understood that a transaction was taking place between them, just like haggling between merchants and customers at a stall. However, at a stall, they were buying goods, while here, they were trading a pawn ticket. The man seemed to have noticed that he was a good potential buyer, deliberately waving the pawn ticket in front of him, as if showing off his wares to attract customers: "Just a fur coat and jewelry, worth over three thousand dollars. Buying the pawn ticket for one and a half yuan is too cheap, isn't it? It won't do. At least you have to add a little more. I really have no choice, I'm too poor, and I can't bear to sell this valuable pawn ticket."

"Then I'll add another ten cents, one yuan sixty cents. I won't add another cent!" A pockmarked man shouted loudly, as if afraid others wouldn't hear, waving his hands, signaling to others to appreciate his generosity, adding ten cents, which was a very bold move.

"You're stealing my business, huh? Fine, I'll add ten cents too!"

The speaker was a burly man, as if in a fit of pique. He glared with his shifty eyes, suggesting that he was a remarkable figure, very masculine.

In Wang Zhanfu's view, the deal should definitely go through this time, because the seller wanted someone to add another bid before selling, and now the price had been raised twice, so he should naturally sell. He watched as the pawn ticket was about to be bought for one yuan seventy cents, as if watching someone win the grand prize. That person was truly fortunate. He shouldn't have watched others easily buy the grand prize. If he had just added another ten cents, he would have made a huge profit. He was a little panicked, afraid that the man would agree to sell the pawn ticket. He couldn't hesitate any longer, determined to join the competition and buy back the grand prize. He couldn't miss this good opportunity at this critical moment.

"Adding so little is not enough," the pawn ticket holder said before he could speak, rejecting the proposed condition. "This amount is not even close, are you joking?" He explained, "Major pawnshops don't pawn bad things. Aren't fur coats and jewelry valuable? Five yuan pawned, plus interest, it's six yuan total. If rich people don't buy it, they won't find such an opportunity again."

"No one said your pawn ticket isn't worth anything," a short person continued, "but once things are sold outside, like pawn tickets and bonds, they really aren't worth much. Do you believe it?"

Wang Zhanfu was secretly calculating. The items listed on the pawn ticket were worth more than twenty yuan, which wasn't much. Even if they were sold at half price, they would still be worth almost twenty yuan. Buying it wouldn't be a loss. He decided to offer two yuan. Wasn't that what the man was hoping for? But he had a cunning plan. He would add money to the man in two installments, as a tactic. Having decided, he mustered his courage and said loudly, "Ah, I'll add another ten cents for you, okay? I can see you need the money urgently, so I'll add ten cents more for you."

His actions seemed to startle everyone present. People looked at him with surprise, and he became a top hero in an unseen way. Sure enough, no one spoke up, and some gave up their bidding rights, turning away to buy cheaper goods with some resentment.

Unexpectedly, someone was still causing trouble for him, the pockmarked man, who, for some inexplicable reason, added another half a dime! This forced him to raise his offer to two yuan, and the transaction was completed to his joyful expectations. He happily walked back. He presented the pawn ticket to his relative, saying joyfully, "Look, I bought something worth thirty or forty yuan for two yuan! What other business has such a big profit? This is my first time in the city, and it's the first time I've made such a profitable deal!"

"Ah, you've been cheated this time," the relative exclaimed after reading the pawn ticket, stamping his feet. "This is a fake ticket! It's a scam designed to trick people. Why were you so meddlesome!"

"Doesn't the ticket have the pawnshop's address, the amount, and the pawned items?" he asked, still not believing it. "How can it be fake when it's written so clearly!"

"That's all fake too. Let me tell you, you've made a losing deal."

He still didn't believe it, thinking that his relative was just teasing him out of jealousy of his good luck. He went to look for the pawnshop at the address stated on the pawn ticket. Once there, he would know whether it was real or fake. He walked back and forth on that street five times, unable to find a pawnshop. It was then that he realized he had been cheated. Thinking of the two yuan that had flown away, he broke into a cold sweat from anxiety and anger, and stood there dumbfounded.

Forms of Life 230

— Liang Qiyun

"Living here isn't bad, is it?" - My introducer, Guo Santa, said to me.

Guo Santa was a short, stout woman in her fifties. She had a compassionate heart, supposedly because of her religious beliefs. She had saved a little money, but was stingy even with small amounts. - Three weeks after I moved into the back room, Chen Shi-nai from the front building chatted with me casually and mentioned these things, without any malicious intent. From her, I also learned the following about my introducer: - Next door lived a witch who worshipped a deity called West Marquis King. She had a large group of devout followers, and Guo Santa was one of her most devout disciples.

I quickly became familiar with my neighbors. Whenever they needed one more person for mahjong, they would never forget Yi. That was how they somehow called me.

Among the gamblers, Xi Boqing, the rubber shoe factory worker in the attic room, was the most interesting character. As long as he was there, everything would become lively. When he played "Two of Bamboo," he would say,

"Give you one!"

People would laugh out loud. The women would blush. I didn't quite understand, but there were probably some obscene words hidden underneath. Sometimes, when he drew a sequence, he would ask himself:

"Oh, should I find a partner?"

I didn't care for that. But everyone welcomed it, and they would burst into laughter. Perhaps they were too lacking in sources of laughter. Yes, people should laugh often. If a troubled life is not harmonized with laughter, life would become unbearably dull, monotonous, and gloomy.

The silent vegetable vendor, Chen Ge, would go to the market as soon as the sky showed a pale grey. In the tense atmosphere of mahjong, he possessed our unique native Chinese characteristics: composure, calmness, and patience. He was a bit nearsighted. Bending his head, his large red nose seemed to be rubbing on the table.

I rarely stayed at home.

"Brother, you inevitably have to be a bit hypocritical. People live just to get by. You should run around outside more. Regardless of whether you're unemployed or not, people will naturally respect you. Moreover, if you hide at home, even if there's gold on the street, you won't know it,"

The brokerage trader Yang Jianchen said to me in a lecturing tone. I had just lost my job then. As he spoke, his nose twitched amusingly, as if exaggerating his "intelligence" and "insight." Every time his nose moved, it seemed to be saying silently:

"See, you're such a clever fellow."

He was indeed too clever.

He committed a crime by smuggling pistols, and was sentenced to a long prison term.

However, what he said did have some meaning.

I should thank him. By spending more time outside, I quickly found a job. It was a street-running job for a fountain pen company. A profession that used a mixture of grandiosity, boasting, and seduction to trick reluctant customers out of their money.

When I was at home, I rarely had free time.

In the evenings, on holidays, I had no streets to run. The neighbors always dragged me into mahjong games. Their daily income was mostly meager, but, strangely, they were all gambling addicts in the third stage of tuberculosis. Like the rubber shoe factory worker, Xi Boqing; the vegetable vendor, Chen Ge; Chen Qibin, the husband of Chen Shi-nai from the front building; and the witch Xu Dagu, who lived by mysterious, deceiving tricks....

Chen Ge was also good at singing "Banben" and reading "Wooden Fish Books." In the narrow room, a group of people would often gather. Their enthusiastic, curious, and doubtful eyes floated over the stale clichés of stories like "Liu Jinding Secretly Investigates the Barracks," "Su Niang Writes a Blood Letter," "Crown Prince Ciyun Flees the Country," and "Hu Sheng's Parting Lament."

I often served as his volunteer advisor. He asked me to explain some of the obscure sentences and the meanings of the unfamiliar, difficult words...

I moved away after living there for a relatively short time.

Forms of life are multifaceted. - Under various forms, many people live.

Battlefield Moon 231

— Wang Yaping

No sound of autumn insects,

The night is desolate.

The moon on the mountaintop, trembling,

Casts a pale white glow.

The leaves have all fallen,

The grass has been trampled.

The bloody wind, from the collapsed

Trenches, blows the dirge of death.

No dog barks, no rooster crows,

Terror locks down the land.

The will-o'-the-wisps of stars fly,

The desolate village sleeps in the ruins.

Moliere's The Miser 232

— Written by Doi Itsuo, Translated by Ouyang Fan Hai

The father of Harpagon was a guy who hid in the small stable to steal feed for his horse. He desperately misses women, but the woman he misses is the lover of his own son, Harpagon.

The sons and daughters are driven by their father's infatuation, so they try many methods and start using money. Harpagon wants to get rid of his father's restraint, create a free love without money, and goes to see a usurer to borrow money, only to find that the usurer is his own father. Here, the old morality that forms the outer shell of the father, son, or family is already powerless. The father scolds the son for being promiscuous, and the son scolds the father for being a beast.

Replaced by the opposition between strong desire and pure love, the typical here is a human being bound by money, who strives to create a new way of life using various primitive methods. This essence of early modern life has continued to develop to this day, and has produced various different forms. Moliere's eyes penetrate deeply into reality, and even our modern hearts are moved from the depths.

Moliere does not use this play to preach to the audience, but there is probably no audience who can watch this play without laughing uncontrollably. Then everyone will think, do such interesting scenes really exist?

The laugh of a miser is indeed like the laugh of a strong and healthy person. We often have to suppress our laughter due to etiquette, even though things are truly laughable. We are in danger of becoming accustomed to suppressing what we want to be angry about and what we want to say.

Moliere's boldness in directly and impolitely ridiculing the ridiculous gives our theater a direction and gives the audience and us a proactive attitude. (The End)

Starting with Moving 233

— Yang

In a place like Shanghai, moving is a rather serious problem for single people. Isn't it true that most rental ads say something like "No Families Allowed"?

I have lived in Shanghai for eight or nine years, and have never had any "family members," nor do I have a job. Every time I move, I feel a headache coming on.

"Family members?" - None.

"So, where do you make your fortune?" - Nowhere.

As a result, I have to see either an embarrassed, honest face or two suspicious, cunning eyes, but the result is the same: I will be politely or impolitely rejected.

Fortunately, this society that requires money for rent and guarantors for tenants has taught people a way to protect themselves: lying.

"My wife will be coming from home in a few days."

"I'm a proofreader at a certain publishing house. I don't need to go to the bookstore, I can work at home..."

Lies like these are the secret to my successful moves every time.

Also, fortunately, I am a very lazy person with a strong inertia. Once I settle in a place, I don't want to move unless the sub-landlord is too oppressive -- such as not allowing the lights to be turned on after midnight -- or when it becomes necessary to move for my own convenience. And when I do move, I don't want to move too far away from the old site, away from those roads where my footprints will be imprinted day and night, the signs of those familiar-but-unfamiliar businesses and shops, and even the men and women on the left and right who seem very familiar but are not known. Speaking of which, my strong inertia has saved me a lot of trouble with moving!

I have been living here for almost a month now. Needless to say, before deciding to move here, I spent a lot of time considering: First, the rent is cheap, only ten yuan a month, including the money for the amah; second, it's quiet, so I can write; third, there's a bathroom, which is very important in the summer; fourth, the food situation, there are Russian restaurants nearby, where a dish, a cup of black tea, and a few slices of bread cost only twenty cents per meal, which is very cost-effective; fifth... In short, I felt that everything was in order, and I happily moved in, telling a lie that I was an editor at a bookstore and worked at home.

Very good! After moving in, on the first day, I discovered a major drawback: I have to run two miles to get food.

I was too careless; but things really change too quickly. Last winter, there were indeed several Russian restaurants in this area, but now there are none left! Although there are restaurants nearby, I have always eaten bread in recent years. What should I do?

There is no way, I still have to live here. First, I really don't want the trouble of "moving"; second, it was not easy to get the ten yuan rent.

Day after day passed, and every day I had to run a long distance four times for food. With the weather as hot as it has been in recent days, it is really a bit miserable. The sweat I shed every day for food will probably make me an even skinnier ghost.

However, this time, almost a month, has made me feel a mysterious emotion towards the things around here. Even the "eating" problem, which I initially felt very troublesome, has gradually improved recently, and I don't feel it is inconvenient anymore, and sometimes I even find it interesting. At first, I decided to move after living here for a month, but now I don't want to move, and it seems like I can live here permanently... Well, that long road I have to run several times a day, those unhealthy trees nailed to the roadside, the dirty but beautifully contoured face of the young clerk at the cigarette shop, the croaking of frogs every night in the quiet of the night, and the flushing toilet that wakes me up every morning, the landlady's clatter... All these things, whether I like them or hate them, have formed an inextricable bond with my life, entangling me, making me unable and unwilling to leave them... Well, if there is no unexpected force pushing me, I am afraid that I can stay here permanently, and just live like this. I feel the distress of my own strong inertia!

Thinking about it, people with strong inertia are not very useful. I lag behind in everything and don't make progress easily. Other people are charging ahead, but I am still standing far behind, clenching my fists, and that's why?

Yes, strong inertia is indeed the biggest problem that prevents people from making progress! For example, like other people, I want women, and I also want to eat. For the past four or five years, I have always thought about women's bodies, but for these five or six years, I have been single. I have neither the opportunity to naturally meet women, nor the courage to snatch other people's "doves," so I have to endure my spring dreams in the so-called "wind and moonlight." One day, two days, one year, two years pass like this, until it becomes a kind of inertia that is not easy for me to move. Unless I encounter a strong stimulation and push, I am afraid that I can live my whole life like this. Eating is the same. When I am hungry, I want to eat, and when I have something to eat, I often want to eat something better. However, ham or something like chicken velvet shark fin will not fall from the sky for you, and I don't have the powerful hand to snatch buttered bread from other people's mouths, so I have to let it be malnourished, and it won't die immediately. One day, two days, one year, two years pass like this, until now I have become accustomed to it, and the poor, salty life has become a kind of inertia that I cannot move. If I suddenly enter a luxurious and extravagant living environment, I will feel uneasy and uncomfortable, and arouse a sense of disgust.

My body should work hard for women and more nutritious food! However, I am content with the status quo and do not seek to make progress. I am useless, my inertia is too strong!

I envy people with weak inertia!

It would be even better to have no inertia!

Well, no inertia...

Well, well...

No inertia? Are there such people in the world?

Yes, what kind of person would that be?

That would be a person that you can't figure out...

That would become the individualistic animal that Gorky called it. For their own benefit, they can change a thousand times in an instant, without thinking...

Isn't that terrible?

Well...

Think about it: still dreaming of visiting the Grand View Garden in the middle of the night, dreaming of entering the Land of Illusion, waking up at three o'clock in the morning, but being a hero like Liangshanbo...

Well, just now it was a flying eagle and a sea swallow, and in the blink of an eye it becomes a pig's head and a dog's face; today it plays a big part, and tomorrow it plays a clown; at this moment it's a righteous person, and the next moment it's a rogue...

If the world were full of people with no inertia or almost no inertia, wouldn't that be too terrible?

Well, well, thinking of this...

It's better for everyone to have a little more inertia!

However, my own inertia is too strong after all, so strong that it is rigid, dull, and non-dialectical...

Okay! I'll move next month!

Red and White Leukorrhea 239

— (Xiao Yun)

Red and white leukorrhea is a disease particularly prevalent among Chinese women. Lack of proper hygiene during menstruation, inadequate postpartum care, and unclean personal hygiene products can all lead to diseases of the uterus and vagina. The result is increased inflammatory secretions. Mild cases involve yellowish-white, sticky substances, known as leukorrhea. In severe cases, ulceration occurs in the internal mucous membrane, and superficial blood vessels are damaged, resulting in secretions mixed with blood, known as red leukorrhea. Some cases of red and white leukorrhea are caused by tumors in the uterine cavity, while others are caused by venereal viruses. Still others are caused by physical weakness, chlorosis, or acute and chronic simple urogenital diseases. Since there is a definite cause for the symptoms of red and white leukorrhea, it is regrettable that many women are often too embarrassed to seek medical attention, delaying treatment and allowing the disease to progress to an incurable state. General Discussion on Gonorrhea in Women 240

— (Yi Ren)

The cause of gonorrhea is the gonococcus, discovered by Neisser in 1879. The most susceptible sites are the urethra and vagina in young girls, and the urethra, cervical canal, and fallopian tubes in women. Gonorrhea is mainly transmitted through sexual intercourse and then spreads upwards, dividing into mild and severe cases. The former is limited to the lower genital tract, i.e., the vulva, vagina, urethra, and cervical canal. The latter also extends to the deeper parts, i.e., the uterine cavity, fallopian tubes, ovaries, and peritoneum. The predisposing factors for ascending infection are as follows: (1) menstruation; (2) puerperium; (3) excessive sexual activity; (4) intrauterine surgery, etc. The clinical findings and symptoms of each site are described below. (1) Acute stage of gonococcal urethritis: There is a burning sensation during urination, often severe pain, and frequent urination. The mucous membrane of the external urethral orifice is congested and swollen, with thick pus-like secretions containing countless gonococci. It usually progresses to the chronic stage after three to four weeks. Once it becomes chronic, the above symptoms almost disappear, the amount of pus-like secretions is greatly reduced, and the external urethral orifice is slightly congested. (2) Gonococcal vulvitis: Limited to young girls, pregnant women, and the elderly. Acute stage: There is an unbearable burning sensation, especially after urination. The labia, clitoris, and hymen become edematous. Thick pus-like secretions are present. The inguinal lymph nodes are often swollen. It progresses to the chronic stage after one to two weeks. The result is the development of condylomata acuminata, resembling a rooster's comb. (3) Acute stage of gonococcal vaginitis: There is a feeling of lower abdominal pain, burning itching, and increased leukorrhea. The mucous membrane is red and swollen, resembling velvet. Pressure causes severe pain. It becomes noticeably milder after two to three weeks. If gonococci are still seen in the secretions, it indicates that they are coming from the cervical canal. (4) Acute stage of cervical gonococcal infection: The pathogens mostly reside in the superficial layer. The vaginal portion of the cervix is severely swollen, leaking greenish-yellow pus-like secretions. The surrounding area is eroded and not very painful. It is only felt upon touching it. Chronic stage: The secretions may be pus-like or mucous. The subjective symptoms are not obvious. Microscopic examination is required to prove the presence of pathogens to confirm that it is gonococcal. (5) Acute stage of gonococcal endometritis: High fever, reaching 38 to 40 degrees Celsius. Severe pain in the lower abdomen. Increased leukorrhea. The uterus is swollen and has severe tenderness. After one week, the symptoms become milder and become chronic, making it difficult to cure. During this period, only a feeling of discomfort is felt in the lower abdomen. It often worsens during menstruation and after labor, often leading to excessive menstruation. The uterus is hard and thickened, making it difficult to conceive. (6) Gonococcal salpingitis: Mostly involves both sides and frequently affects the peritoneum, so the symptoms are quite complex. Acute stage: The affected side has stabbing pain. Fever. Menstrual abnormalities. The affected fallopian tube is swollen and tortuous like a snake. Chronic stage: The symptoms are reduced. It often worsens during menstruation and after labor. Lower back pain, lower abdominal pain, are almost inevitable. Gastrointestinal disturbances. General malnutrition. The nervous system is greatly affected. (7) Gonococcal oophoritis and pelvic peritonitis: Acute stage: There is lower abdominal pain. Nausea, vomiting, abdominal distension. Fever. Constipation or diarrhea. Rapid and weak pulse. Chronic stage: The symptoms are greatly relieved, but it often recurs. Fertility is completely hopeless. Therefore, the prognosis of this disease depends on the timeliness of treatment and the location of the lesions. Fifty percent of infertility is actually caused by this disease. It is said that gonorrhea in women is mostly transmitted by their husbands. Men who frequent prostitutes contract gonorrhea and either keep it a secret without seeking treatment or do not receive radical treatment, inevitably infecting their wives. Therefore, both husband and wife must undergo radical treatment together. Otherwise, if the husband is treated but the wife is not, or the wife is treated but the husband is not, they will transmit it to each other, causing endless harm. However, it is often inconvenient for women to seek medical attention, so self-treatment is still available. The internal Leukorrhea Pills and external Leukorrhea Medicine sold by Father and Son Hospital at No. 64 Ningbo Road in the French Concession of Shanghai can radically cure gonorrhea in women. The price is two yuan per box for the internal medication and two yuan per box for the external medication. When used together, they will quickly cure the condition. These two medications not only treat gonorrhea in women but also have miraculous effects on common leukorrhea. Many women who are chlorotic and infertile due to leukorrhea have had their complexions turn from pale to rosy after being treated with these products, and they have also been blessed with offspring. It is truly the only good medicine for women.

Discussions

My Thoughts on the Olympic Games 242

— Fang Kewen

From August 1st onwards, the news about the Olympic Games has been quite lively in the newspapers. Until today, when the newspaper published "Basketball Also Eliminated, Our Team Completely Annihilated, The Games Have Nothing to Do With Us," I think most Chinese people who read the newspaper cannot help but take a look. After that, because of the "complete annihilation" and because it has nothing to do with us, it will inevitably cool down, right?

As for me, to be honest, I am not very enthusiastic about the Olympic Games. I do read the news about the Olympics, but it's not much different from looking at movie listings. The reason is not because I know that our team will definitely get a duck egg, so I don't get excited. In fact, it's because I still don't believe that the Olympic Games will benefit "world peace," or even "small enough," that it will benefit our Chinese sports, or that it will benefit the physical fitness of our Chinese people.

Speaking of the word "China," I think its correct meaning should refer to the entire Chinese population. However, what is the Chinese people's enjoyment of sports? Not to mention the people in poor and remote areas, even in Shanghai, where the sports atmosphere is the most enthusiastic, how many people can truly enjoy it?

To put it bluntly, or rather, to be honest, our watching track and field, our watching ball games, is almost like going to the Canidrome or the theater. We just go to appreciate it, and those who "play" sports seem to want to create a few "sports stars" like "ball king" or "mermaid," but besides that, it doesn't seem to be for anything else.

In this way, I think it's okay that our Olympic team returns with a duck egg. Winning wouldn't be anything glorious either, because even if we brought back a bunch of gold medals, it would still have nothing to do with our pallid people.

Of course, while reading the newspaper, I can't help but feel some sorrow about the "complete annihilation" of our team. But this feeling is very simple. It's just because those who were once famous and powerful in our country, such as the "mermaid," etc., were held, welcomed, and entertained without any neglect in the country, and some even condescended to coach them. When they went abroad, they were eliminated in the preliminaries, and most of the athletes were not only unqualified in the field events, but also always the last one to arrive in the preliminary races. When we went, we certainly intended to return with a duck egg, but it doesn't seem like we traveled all the way there just to run a hundred meters at the Olympic Games and then return, right? It doesn't seem like we intended to run "last" in the "preliminaries," right?

Secondly, what the Olympic Games gave me was a factual answer to the absurd theory of white people being superior to everything else, which was advocated by Mr. Hitler and his ilk. We will not forget the arrogance of Mr. Hitler and his ilk when they massacred Jews and advocated that colored people were inferior. But what about now? The American athlete Owens, who won three first places, is a colored "black man." This colored person, who has always been looked down upon by Mr. Hitler and his ilk, won three championships in a single Olympics. This is unprecedented in the history of the Olympic Games. And Son Kitei, who won the marathon, is a Korean, a so-called "slave of a subjugated nation" who is despised!

We cite the above examples not to say that colored people are superior to white people. We are not that absurd. On the contrary, we want to prove that there is no distinction between the races in the world.

Because of this "sports national humiliation," I heard that our authorities are preparing to set up a sports school dedicated to training athletes. The location is planned to be at the sports field, and the quota is 1,000 people each time. In order to "win glory for the country" and to "avenge the shame," their ambition is commendable. However, what use is it to train a group of star system sports stars, except to show off at the Olympic Games (whether it is possible is another question)? What benefit is it to the entire China? At this critical moment of national survival, there seem to be so many "urgent matters" that we need to do. It seems that these national decorations do not need to be studied urgently. Otherwise, even if we train them, even if we get points at the Olympic Games, it is just another Owens, just another Son Kitei. What does it have to do with our China?

Road 243

— Meng Hua

——Sending Mr. Wang to Japan

Now, you have finally left. Leaving behind a family that is entering its twilight years, leaving behind a lonely and helpless wife, bravely holding a golden hope, crossing the vast and dangerous ocean, you are so determined. You have left!

I don't want to use words about how dangerous the waves are or how harsh foreign countries are to travelers like you to stop you. Everything is like a headwind, and you are like a kite. You like headwinds so much. The wind comes strong, and you rise higher. I know that all the suffering, although it has tested you, it will not make you retreat. Friend, just move forward!

What a treacherous road you have traveled in the past twenty-five years! But you have finally overcome all the dangers. The layers of wrinkles on your face are your scars. In this world, how difficult it is to establish our ideals! What is a small physical injury?

You are from Sichuan, so you must have passed through the Three Gorges of the Yangtze River. You will not forget the natural dangers of the Qutang Gorge and Baidi City! Here, I am not describing the simple beauty of nature to you. I want you to pay attention to the great artificial structures, the paths carved out of the dangerous rocks and cliffs on both sides of the river. You will not forget them, will you? They are carved so wide and so long. People who do not have much faith in life cannot imagine this, but the brave pioneers finally used cones and chisels to laboriously carve out the "road," providing a path for millions of people to walk on. Isn't the road of life the same? You have seen such a great project, you should value yourself and increase your infinite courage! What dangers can't people overcome?

You, no, we have all come to a dense, thorny, and primitive forest. For ourselves, for our future generations of children and grandchildren, we must muster courage and open up a path for them. There was originally no "road" in the world. It was only after human beings invested their heart and soul and energy to open it up that there was a "road." You should make good use of yourself, take out an axe, and use your own strength to open up a path!

You have left, and I have no gifts to send you. I will use these few words to give you a farewell. This is the burning heart of your loving friend. Keep it with you and go to a foreign country!

May the waves be even more ferocious, they can make you more courageous to move forward! Go, my friend!

Leaky Roof 244

— Yun

I woke up in the middle of the night and heard a faint pitter-patter sound near the window. Three days ago, the glass window in the side room was broken by a thief with a diamond drill, and many things were stolen. Although my room only has a few piles of broken books and newspapers, and a few pieces of worthless furniture, if there really is a thief who visits, I am not afraid that he will steal anything. But if a fierce-looking (let's assume) man suddenly jumps in from the window, shines a flashlight in all directions, and finally discovers a waking owner lying in bed and staring at him, I might encounter a greater danger than just having a few things stolen! Thinking this, I quickly turned on the flashlight and shone it on the glass window. Outside the window, there were light rain threads, and dew-like raindrops were condensed on the glass window. There was no shadow of a thief. But the pitter-patter sound continued, which surprised me. So, from one corner to another, I carefully patrolled the small room. Finally, I found water stains leaking from the roof on the wall near the window. The leaking place was right above a bookshelf and piles of old newspapers. That sound was the sound of rainwater leaking onto the newspapers.

Those worthless things were my precious property. I immediately jumped out of bed. The bookshelf was placed in the air, so it was not damaged. The pile of newspapers was piled along the base of the wall, and it happened to become a reservoir for the leaking roof. From the top one to the bottom one, they were all soaked with water. I was stuck to you, and you were stuck to me. There was no way to separate them. Even if I wanted to move them, it was impossible. If it kept dripping until dawn, I don't know what the pile of newspapers would become. I was heartbroken that the pile of newspapers that had been with me for years, moving east and west, was completely sacrificed in a few hours.

The next day, I told the landlord about the situation last night. They had already called a plumber. It turned out that it was not only my room that was invaded by the trickle of water. It was harassing everywhere and making people uneasy. The attic had almost become a watery country. All the washbasins and foot stoves were filled with rainwater.

Two plumbers came. They spent the whole day repairing the leaks on the roof and replacing hundreds of new tiles. It rained again yesterday, and I paid attention to the leaking place. At first, there was a circular water stain, which gradually grew larger, and finally it dripped again. I asked in other houses, and there were still many places where it was dripping.

The landlord scolded the plumbers for making a mess. He called two more. They looked at the roof wearing straw hats and said that the house itself was too old, the oak wood had been hollowed out by termites, the rainwater could no longer walk along the tiles, and all the rafters were soaked with water.

The landlord was stunned. He said, "This ring is not mine. The main landlord is unwilling to renovate. The rent is cheap, so let's just be a little careless."

The tenants who suffered losses had nothing to say. The second landlord had fulfilled his responsibility as a second landlord. To repair the house itself, one had to negotiate with the main landlord, but the rent was cheap, so the main landlord's calculations definitely did not include the status of the third tenants. They only had their own interests!

I turned the bookshelf around, and reluctantly threw the pile of newspapers into the trash can. From now on, whenever I see it raining outside, I worry that there will suddenly be several more leaky places in this house, or right above my bed, so that I cannot sleep peacefully.

But when will the main landlord be willing to take out his wallet to renovate this house?

Storytelling in Song 246

Cao Xiaoxiao's Jade Dragonfly

China & West (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening: "New Baoyu Visits the Sick"

The Hong Mansion's Young Master and Miss Lin. Growing up together, they each harbored affection. Unexpectedly, Heaven grew jealous, afflicting the beauty with illness, trapping her in a city of sorrow. Her delicate form lay in the Xiaoxiang Pavilion, while her little maid often brewed medicinal tea. Sighing, she lamented the lack of kindred spirits, her heart moved, tears filling her eyes. Suddenly, the parrot called out repeatedly, saying a guest was knocking, calling for the maid named Juan. Hastily, she ordered the maid to go outside the room to ask who had come, wanting to hear clearly. The maid obeyed, opening the door, and was immediately moved to see it was Baoyu. Because his coming late at night was a rare event, it showed that his affection and righteousness were naturally formed. She hurriedly took the lantern and guided him inside with light steps. Reaching the bedside, she reported, "Young Master Baoyu has come alone tonight. He has come in person to visit you in your illness. I have sincerely welcomed him on your behalf. He has arrived at your bedside to see you. You may ask him to judge any grievances you have." Daiyu listened, feeling a multitude of emotions. It was as if she had seen the sun after a long rain. She had a thousand words to say, but where to begin? She barely managed to softly call out, "Cousin." Saying, "Second Aunt is truly too much. I am full of sorrow and sickness, I am about to be angered to death. Although the Old Ancestor treats me kindly, when I am ill, I ultimately cannot express my grievances. Do not hope that my body can recover without medicine; I fear we will only meet again in the next life to pledge our vows." Baoyu listened, alarmed in his heart, and advised her not to argue with the Wang family. He urged her to take care of her body to ensure her well-being, to put all matters aside, and to hope for good fortune. After offering his advice, he bid farewell. He could hardly make a sound of injustice. He could only sing these few lines as the opening.

He Yunfang and He Qinfang's Twin Pearl Ballads

Lin Kee (1220) 2:15 PM to 3:00 PM

Opening: "The Word 'Spring'"

Trickling spring water drips in the mountains. Everyone says the Immortal Cliff's spring water is connected. Baotu Spring has many ancient sites. The hidden hermit enjoys endless joy from forests and springs. Listening to the spring is better than listening to the pines. Mountain valleys and singing springs are the work of creation. The spring water of Huishan in Wuxi is wonderfully mysterious. The flying spring resembles ancient snow in the depths of winter. The fragrant spring is incomparably rich. Don't say Dragon Spring turns into a dragon. The Spear Method of Li Quan is incredibly strange. Jade Spring Mountain presenting sages is always empty. Su Laoquan, the Elder Su of Quan. He only began to exert himself at the age of twenty-seven. Truly, he was a great Confucian scholar of the Song Dynasty. There is much delight between springs and rocks.
